Primary School Holiday Homework Achievement Exhibition 206

Held at Wanzhu Primary School on October 20th

Methods, Rules, and Evaluation Standards Announced Yesterday

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education instructed all municipal and registered private primary schools in the city, "The methods for the Shanghai Municipal Primary School Holiday Homework Achievement Exhibition jointly organized by this bureau and the Shanghai Children's Morning Post, the rules of the preparatory committee, and the standards for evaluating competition results have been drafted separately and submitted to the 290th bureau affairs meeting for discussion, all of which have been approved. They should be announced and implemented immediately. Furthermore, the product catalog and labels have now been printed and should be collected from the bureau immediately. The product form must be completed and sent to the bureau ten days before the meeting. This order, together with a copy of the above-mentioned methods, rules, and standards, is hereby issued for your school to follow."

Exhibition Methods 207

(1) This bureau and the newspaper are formulating these methods in accordance with Article 12 of the Shanghai Municipal Primary School Holiday Homework Competition Rules. (2) The Shanghai Municipal Primary School Holiday Homework Achievement Exhibition (hereinafter referred to as "this exhibition") will be implemented in accordance with these methods. (3) All municipal primary schools and registered private primary schools in Shanghai may select and submit the holiday homework achievements of students in the third grade and above for display in this exhibition in accordance with the provisions of these methods. (4) The exhibits sent to this exhibition by each school are limited to this year's summer vacation homework, the scope of which is as follows: A. The competition results organized by the Shanghai Children's Morning Post. B. Homework materials determined by each school. (5) The venue of this exhibition is located at Shanghai Municipal Wanzhu Primary School. (6) The exhibition period of this exhibition is set for October 20th. (7) The arrangement of the exhibits of each school shall be the responsibility of the teachers and staff of each school. (8) The exhibits sent to this exhibition by each school shall be sent to the venue of this exhibition within three days before the opening. (9) During the exhibition period, each school shall assign several teachers and staff to be responsible for the safekeeping of the exhibits and to explain doubts to visitors and judges. (10) Each school shall prepare a catalog of exhibits and submit it to this exhibition for record before the meeting. The catalog format will be determined separately by this exhibition. (11) The exhibits of each school shall be classified by grade and subject for display, and an exhibit label shall be attached to the exhibit. The format will be determined separately by this exhibition. (12) The exhibits of each school shall be returned by the school itself within one day after the exhibition period. (13) All preparatory matters of this exhibition will be planned and carried out by a separate preparatory committee, and the methods will be determined separately. (14) If there are any shortcomings in these methods, the preparatory committee may revise them at any time. (15) These methods will be implemented from the date of announcement.

Preparatory Committee Rules 208

(1) This exhibition is jointly organized by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education and the Shanghai Children's Morning Post. The Preparatory Committee for the Shanghai Municipal Primary School Holiday Homework Achievement Exhibition will be established to prepare for the Shanghai Municipal Primary School Holiday Homework Achievement Exhibition. (2) This committee will have five members and several staff members, who will be appointed separately by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education and the Shanghai Children's Morning Post. (3) The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education will appoint one of the members to be the chairman of the committee, responsible for presiding over the committee affairs. (4) The powers of this committee are as follows: 1. Collection of exhibits, 2. Printing and distribution of exhibit forms and catalogs, 3. Arrangement of the venue, 4. Hiring of venue staff, 5. Closing of the exhibition after the event, 6. Other matters related to the preparation of the exhibition. (5) The office of this committee is temporarily located at the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, but it should be moved to the venue if necessary. (6) The funds required for this committee will be submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education for allocation after preparing the budget. (7) The meeting of this committee will be convened by the chairman. (8) These rules will be implemented from the date of announcement.

Evaluation Standards 209

(A) Fifth and Sixth Grades: (1) Chinese Language: 20%, (2) Arithmetic: 20%, (3) Social Studies: 20%, (4) Natural Science: 20%, (5) Art: 20%. (B) Third and Fourth Grades: (1) Chinese Language: 20%, (2) Arithmetic: 20%, (3) Social Studies: 20%, (4) Natural Science: 20%, (5) Art: 20%.

Liu Wendao's Speech at Jinan University: Six Meanings of Italian Revival 211

Our country's ambassador to Italy, Mr. Liu Wendao, at 3 p.m. yesterday, at the invitation of the National Jinan University in Zhenru, came to the university to give a speech. Upon arrival, he was personally led by the university president, Shen Pengfei, to the Zhiyuan Hall of the university. More than a thousand students attended. The main points of his speech are recorded below. Mr. Liu first pointed out that since the European War, among the countries in Central Europe that have revived, there are Turkey, Italy, and Germany. Having been stationed in Germany for two years and in Italy for one year, I am relatively familiar with the political situation of the two countries. I feel that Italy was in extreme disorder before and after the European War, with frequent natural disasters and wars. The degree of internal and external troubles was worse than that of China today. However, since Mussolini seized power by force and used democracy to govern, he has won the sympathy of the people nationwide and astonished the world by looking down on everything. In fact, Mussolini's success, although not easy, also has an indelible spirit underlying it. The greatest banner, to warn and encourage people, is the Six Meanings: (1) Order: When Italy was in extreme turmoil, he saw clearly that the most important prerequisite was to calm people's hearts and restore the inherent order of the country. Therefore, his personal life and behavior were especially cautious in word and deed to set an example for the people. It is necessary to rectify one's own heart before one can cultivate oneself, manage one's family, govern the country, and bring peace to the world. Otherwise, if the father is not kind and the son is not filial, and one person implicates a family or a country, it is truly one person eating misfortune and a country causing chaos. Moreover, keeping order is not surrendering to someone, but cultivating civic habits and fulfilling national obligations; (2) Authority: After social stability, there is a need for authority everywhere. The so-called authority is not relying on bullying neighbors, but people being able to do their best, not fearing threats, and being loyal to their duties. It is difficult to say in China where the spirit of the rule of law has not been established, but it can be done in Italy, and it can be seen from a certain thing; (3) Justice; (4) Faith; (5) Obedience; (6) Struggle; These are the great meanings. In short, they are all a consistent policy with a chain-like nature. First, there must be order, then there will be authority. With authority, one can naturally uphold justice and gain people's faith. When the words are correct and things are in order, the world will follow the orders, and then one can talk about struggle, embracing a view of life that completes personality, until one has exhausted one’s efforts and dies. Finally, he explained in detail that revival lies in education, and he greatly encouraged the students of the university. The meeting ended at half past four.

Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Comparative View of the Classification of New Vacuum Tubes 222

— Ming Xiang

Vacuum tubes are increasing day by day, and there are many types. Comrades who like to make radios often have no way to choose. In fact, vacuum tubes commonly used in AC machines can be divided into two categories according to their filament voltage: 2.5v and 6.3v. Many of the characteristics of vacuum tubes between these two categories are quite similar or similar. Now, according to their structural characteristics, they are classified and compared.

(1) Triode: Starting with the triode, in the 2.5v category, there are 27 and 56, which can be equivalent to 37 and 76 in the 6.3v category. Except for the different filament voltage and current, the characteristics and functions of 56 and 76 are completely the same. As for 27 and 37, there are slight differences. The cathode of 37 is smaller, and its transconductance and screen current are also slightly weaker, but in actual design, the effect is completely regarded as the same.

(2) Double-Plate Triode (Diode_Priode): A double-plate triode is an ordinary triode with an additional pair of plates. In the 2.5v category, there are 55 and 2A6, and in the 5.3v category, there are 85 and 75, which can be equivalent to each other, and their characteristics are completely the same. The only difference between 55 and 2A6 is that the amplification coefficient of 55 is 8.3, while that of 2A6 is 100. Therefore, if a larger output power is required, it is advisable to use 2A6.

(3) Constant Power Tetrode and Pentode: The main task of this type of vacuum tube is the first and second detector tubes of the superheterodyne machine. In the 2.5v category, there are 24 and 57. In the 6.3v category, those that can be equivalent to them are 36, 6C6 and 77. 36 and 24 are tetrodes. Except that the cathode of 36 is smaller and the power consumption of the filament is weaker, other characteristics and effects are quite similar to 24; 57, 77, and 6C6 are all pentodes. There are many structural differences between 77 and 6C6, but the electrical characteristics are still completely consistent. For example, the internal isolation of 77 surrounds the plate, while the isolation of 6C6 is above the plate; Although the advantage of the internal isolation of 77 can reduce the isolation device of the radio, the output capacitance also increases at the same time, which is quite unfavorable for high-frequency circuits.

(4) Variable Power Tetrode and Pentode: This type of vacuum tube is most suitable for the high-frequency amplification or intermediate-frequency amplification stage of a radio. In the 2.5v category, there are fewer types, only 35 and 58. 35 is actually the same as 24, and 58 is similar to 57. The only difference is that the former has a variable power effect. In the 6.3v category, those that can be equivalent to it are 39, 44, 6D6, and 78. The variable power effect of is weaker than that of 35. Because 39 is specially designed for car radios, the intensity of its input signal is not as comparable to that of indoor radios equipped with large antennas. The characteristics of 78 are between 39 and 6D6, and 44 can be regarded as completely the same as 39 and can be interchanged. All of the above tubes, except 35, have a suppression grid and become pentodes.

(5) Special Vacuum Tube: Also known as Combination Tube, it is also a type of complex vacuum tube. In the 2.5v category, there are 2A7 and 2B7, and in the 5.3v category, there are 6A7 and 6B7, which are equivalent to them. 6A7 is often used as a frequency converter for superheterodyne machines, and there is another grid dedicated to oscillation, so there is no need to set up an oscillation tube. 2B7 and 6B7 are both double-plate pentodes. The double-plate can be used for detection, and the pentode part is suitable for audio frequency or intermediate frequency amplification.

(6) High-Power Output Tube: There are many types of high-power output tubes in the 2.5v category. 45, 2A3, and 46 are all filament triodes. 2A3 is better than 45 because it can output greater power and the distortion is extremely small. When 46 is used for Class A amplification, its output is smaller than 45. If it is used for Class B amplification, it is stronger than 45, but the distortion is greater than 2A3. 47 and 2A5 are pentode power amplifier tubes, and their characteristics are very similar, but the latter is a cathode type, which can greatly reduce AC noise. In this respect, it seems to be better than 47. In addition, there is No. 59, which has the effects of both 47 and 46. Because there are three grids connected to the outside of the tube, only the connection method of the circuit needs to be changed to suit a certain function. There are only three high-power output tubes in the 6.3v category: 42, 4I, and 89. The characteristics of 42 and 2A5 are the same, and the output of 4I is only slightly weaker. As for 39, it can be regarded as a small 59, because its characteristics and effects are mostly the same.

A Reason for Loud Screaming 223

— Zhu Ziyuan

Recently, a friend installed a three-tube radio. The vacuum tubes used were one 33 detector and two 30 low-frequency amplifiers. The whole machine, except for the battery, was installed in a beautiful wooden box. Unexpectedly, after installation, the screaming sound continued. Therefore, the primary PB of the low-frequency transformer was swapped, but the result was ineffective. Later, I suspected that the grid circuit and the plate circuit were connected in parallel. After careful inspection, I reconnected the suspicious places, and the problem was solved. However, when the radio was put into the box, it still screamed, but when it was taken out of the box, the screaming stopped. Therefore, I decided that the screaming must be related to the loudspeaker (because the loudspeaker was installed in the box). However, the loudspeaker was in the upper part of the box, and the radio was in the lower part of the box, and there was a considerable distance from the transformer, so the screaming would not be caused by the matching. After careful observation, I discovered the reason. It turned out that the wiring on the loudspeaker was too long and was not tied up, and it happened to fall on the grid capacitor and grid leak. Therefore, the plate circuit and the grid circuit produced screaming due to matching. At that time, I tied up the remaining wires on the loudspeaker (that is, the speaker wires), and the screaming was gone. Therefore, when we install the loudspeaker and the radio together, we must also pay attention to the wires on the loudspeaker.

DC Generator with Automatic Output Voltage Regulation 224

— Yi Zhi

In a Class B amplifier, the grid voltage should not be supplied by the electrical source; because the fluctuating grid current flows back into the generator, it easily causes the power supply to change, and the grid voltage cannot be stabilized, resulting in poor operation. If you want to reduce its voltage change, there are only two methods: one is to connect a low-impedance shunt at the output; and the other is to keep the load constant. However, using a low-impedance shunt results in excessive power loss, which is too uneconomical; therefore, the second method should be discussed, which is to keep the load constant, and its change is almost zero.

As shown in the figure, it is a DC generator with automatic output voltage regulation. The difference between it and an ordinary DC generator, in addition to the rectifier tube and filter device, is that it has a Regulation Vocuum_Tube, referred to as a regulation tube; and a self-grid resistor RI, whose value must be several million ohms, so that the regulation tube cuts off the plate current when there is no load. The output voltage is equal to the total voltage of the generator minus the voltage required for the regulation tube to have a cutoff plate current.

If this generator is used in a Class B amplifier to supply the grid voltage, the current flows back into the regulation tube, and the tube then has a grid current; therefore, the voltage passing through the regulation tube increases, and the voltage from the self-grid resistor RI decreases. The sum of the voltage drops between the regulation tube and the RI resistor must be equal to the total voltage of the power supply; Since the voltage of RI decreases, the grid voltage of the regulation tube decreases, which reduces the total plate impedance. The output voltage connected across it is controlled by this, and does not change with the load, so it can be kept constant.

If this device is used in a Class B amplifier to supply a stable plate voltage, its circuit is the same as the above-mentioned control grid voltage. However, the RI value is reduced so that the current passing through the regulation tube when there is no external load is exactly twice the highest average load current.

When an external load is connected, the current passing through the self-grid resistor RI increases. Since the grid voltage of the regulation tube increases, the plate current decreases; therefore, the external load current can be increased. One decrease and one increase cancel each other out, so that the output voltage can be kept constant.

Small Experiences

A Simple Method for Grounding 225

— Yi

One day, a classmate, Wu Jun, asked me to install an antenna and ground wire for him. He was a boarder and had obtained permission from the school authorities, so he installed an antenna (about 75 feet long) on the balcony of the three-story building. After the antenna was installed, he had to install the ground wire. However, the tap was far away from the dormitory (also far away from the lead pipe of the tap). The iron bars were also damaged by the students. I happened to see a big tree outside the window. The branches were very close to the window. I had a whim and thought that the tree had conductivity. So I tied a copper wire to the branch and connected it to the radio for listening. The result was indeed good. So today I write it out for your reference.

Alsea's Latest Invention: Shortwave Antenna 226

In recent years, the sales of shortwave radios have become increasingly popular. In order to eliminate noise and increase efficiency, radio listeners in all sectors attach great importance to the improvement of antennas. In view of this, Alsea Victory Company specially conducted in-depth research by its experienced technicians and invented a new type of home antenna, called "Alsea's Latest Antenna." It can receive radio waves from the sea, land, and air. The installation is simple and can be used in every household. The method uses a double-crossover wire equipment. The efficiency of receiving long and short wave radio signals is several times higher than that of ordinary antennas. Even if the lead-in wire of the radio is more than 500 feet long, the receiving efficiency is still not reduced. It can also avoid the noise generated by this lead-in wire. A switch is installed inside the radio, which is specially used to change the reception of broadcast and shortwave programs. Therefore, after all long and short wave radios are retrofitted with this new Alsea antenna, the receiving performance will definitely be improved. The performance of old-fashioned shortwave radios with adapters is also good when using this antenna. In addition, if the roof area is too small to install a long enough antenna, you can also retrofit this new type of antenna, and you can get the same effect.

Little Western Paradise 227

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: Entering Trade into the Folk, Returning to Yongshou, Leaving Home, and Arriving in Chang'an

The girl bit her four front teeth on her sleeve, and just looked at the ground with her head down. Jia Duocai suddenly changed his mind, it was all his fault. Since he admired this girl very much, how could he make her too embarrassed? So he said to the old woman: Since you have also arrived in Xi'an, that's very good. You can always think of a way slowly. Where do you live? The middle-aged woman glanced at Jia Duocai and took a step back, clearly having something to say, but suddenly she was shy and endured it back. It was the old woman who saw that this old master was not unintentional, so she interjected: This child's father is there, we have not received any information. This child's uncle has also gone there, but the aunt is here, and we live there. This child's aunt took us out to see, we felt like we had arrived in the Heavenly Palace, and we were reluctant to go back, so she left first. Now we are in trouble, not knowing how to go home. Jia Duocai said: Where do your relatives live? I'll take you back. The old woman supported the trunk of the tree and thought with her head raised: What alley? The middle-aged woman shook her head at her and said: No! I remember it's in Heaven. Jia Li and the two couldn't help but laugh. The middle-aged woman blushed and smiled: No, no, it's something-Heaven behind. The girl couldn't bear it any longer, so she turned her head and glared at them and said: Your memories are really bad, isn't it No. 8 Wangjia Alley behind Little Western Paradise? You don't even remember this little thing, what people are you looking for? Jia Duocai said: That's great, we live in Little Western Paradise, we'll lead you back along the way. The two women didn't say yes or no, but just took two steps back, meaning to let Jia Li and the two move forward. Jia Duocai nodded and said: Follow me. (34)

Wang Renqiu's Shanghai Observations 228

— Yanqiao

Forty-five years ago, during the Guangxu fifteenth year, the writer Wang Renqiu was going to Tianjin to see Li Hongzhang, and he passed through Shanghai. (At that time, the Beijing-Hankou Railway had not yet been built, but there were already steamships sailing in the Yangtze River, so he took a detour to Shanghai.) He stayed for several days. Looking at his diary, there are a few things that can show what kind of ideas the old gentleman had about Shanghai.

"Arrived at Dan Gui Yuan, the lantern show was quite elaborate and lively." The previous day he had already been to Tianxian Yuan to watch a show, and later he went there again, which shows that he was a hedonist, and also that he was an outsider, so he only appreciated their craft and liveliness, unlike Luo Yinggong and Li Shikan, who had insider views all their lives.

"Jin Jie came to speak of the evils of compradors, saying that scholars and merchants cannot be friends, let alone compradors, who are barbarian slaves, and scholars associate with them, which is very contrary to propriety. This statement agrees with me, but it does not agree with the current situation." Because someone invited Wang Renqiu to accompany a steamship comprador for dinner during the day, he did not go. This argument is ridiculously pedantic. Which scholar did not associate with compradors later? But the old gentleman was still clear-headed, saying that it did not agree with the current situation, which was a cut above Mr. Jin Jie.

"Entered the New North Gate to the City God Temple... Exited the city to see the Big Self-Ringing Bell, then left and returned. The streets and houses in Shanghai are narrow and dark, still showing the system of a remote and desolate county, and there are also many people in the city, not knowing where to accommodate them?" This is what he meant regarding the inner city of Shanghai. At that time, it was indeed very "narrow and dark," but he wondered how so many people could make a living? He was indeed a person who cared about people's livelihood. If he took the train to Shanghai now, and saw the many luxurious hotels, he would be even more surprised where so many big spenders came from!

"The storyteller and nine prostitutes sang six songs in the library, spending 200 copper coins, which seemed very cheap. No game is so inexpensive for the wealthy." It was probably the female storytellers on the Four Horses Road. Their living standards were only like this more than forty years ago. Even the Qinglian Pavilion now only costs two dimes. How could Mr. Wang already think it was incredibly cheap?

Although these things are very trivial, there have been many changes in the meantime. If you tell them to the young people now, they will already think they are strange tales. If you flip through today's chronicles in a few decades, I'm afraid they will be regarded as ancient historical materials, right?

There are many literati, but no one commemorates or knows them.

Toilet Literature 230

— Fufan

Anyone who sees this topic will definitely think that I am linking "toilet" and "literature" together, insulting the dignity of literature and provoking the resentment of writers. But I don't care about these things at all. The dignity of literature and the lofty status of writers cannot prevent the existence of toilet literature. Look at all the schools now, as long as there are toilets, which one is not painted all over with dazzling colors, a truly magnificent sight?

We know that a certain kind of literature always has a certain style and flavor, but the toilet literature in schools has undergone a thorough liberation. You can write whatever you want, without any system or external constraints. Inside, it contains the eight-legged essay passed down from our ancestors, as well as the new poems that modern people must learn; there are concise plans for national salvation, and vivid anti-Japanese slogans; there are monthly evaluations of empresses and young ladies, and romantic histories of young masters; there are declining and gorgeous love letters, and interesting stories from mulberry fields and paths; there are vulgar and disgusting nicknames from the countryside, and terms commonly used by Dr. Zhang Jingsheng; there are funny game sketches, and humorous satirical texts; there are records of the merits and demerits of the principals and faculty, and complimentary and derogatory words for celebrities and big shots; there are unheard-of secret messages, and unseen novel theories; there are stimulating books, and riddles that are difficult to solve; there is pointed philosophy, and the art of scolding people. ... There is ...

Someone said: "The toilet is a natural and truthful opinion box for students." I think this is correct, so I now have a suggestion, which is that educators who want to examine a school should start from the hidden places. It is best to lower their status and inspect the toilets once. Then, regarding the students' grades, thoughts, and opinions in the school, they can get a concise outline.

Hunting that Disrupts Order 231

Countryside 232

— Zhu Shoutong

At dusk, the setting sun was as red as blood, dyeing half the sky, like a girl's light drink, with a delicate blush on her cheeks; far away, it set off a few clusters of green trees, making it feel particularly lovely. From here, the chirping of sparrows could be heard. Occasionally, one or two would rush out of the treetops and fly away very quickly.

The leaves of poplars and Chinese parasol trees could not withstand the repeated wind and rain, and they all left the branches, danced in the air, and scattered on the roadsides around them. Stepping forward on these fallen leaves made a subtle sound. Looking up at the blue sky, a lone goose carried a mournful cry, and with a lonely heart, slowly flew to its resting place. A faint horn sound was carried by the wind into the eardrum, stirring up my indescribable melancholy. How could a wandering wanderer, with a heart full of wounds, endure the assault of this weeping reed pipe sound?

The reeds by the pool spit out white flowers, trembling in the wind, thin and pitiful. In front, under the fence, one or two remaining flowers could be seen, adorning this desolate countryside.

This area is full of sheep intestines-like paths, without the rumbling of cars disturbing the clear air; nor are there the footprints of enchanting women imprinted on this fragrant soil. At the time when smoke is rising from the cooking stoves, there are only farmers shouldering iron hoes, singing casually, happily walking home with big steps.

Small Recipes

Luoyang Exotic Flavor Records (Part 1) 233

— Zhang Huang

Luodian, also known as Luoxi, or Luoyang, my hometown, is the first town under the jurisdiction of Baoshan County. This town is located in the western countryside, bordering Jiading County. The feng shui is clear and beautiful, the customs are simple and beautiful, outstanding people are born from time to time, and it is also rich in natural resources. Just talking about the food, Luodian has many delicious things that are not available elsewhere. When the west wind rises, I can't help but think of perch soup and minced perch. I will talk about the flavors of my hometown here, tirelessly and as if enumerating family treasures. If any gourmand is greatly moved by this, he can immediately go to the Sun Temple in northern Shanghai, take the Shanghai-Tai long-distance bus, and arrive in Luodian in less than an hour to taste the exotic flavors in person, and take a tour of the town. It is also a pleasure. Now, Sun Zhang Danshi and other village elders are planning to build Luoyang Park. I have also been promoted as a sponsor. When the park is completed in the near future, Shanghai people will be able to go there for a short trip to clear their minds, eat their fill, and return home even more happily! Luodian's food is simply too beautiful to take in. Let me list a few things to serve as a little drool-inducing material:

1. Tea Dish Category

Braised Mutton The tea dishes listed here are those that Luodian families are good at cooking in their daily lives. The wonderful thing about their braised mutton is that it is not fishy or gamey at all. The cooking is done to the point where the meat is crispy but not mushy, the soup is thick and sticky, and the taste is rich, fresh, and sweet! The dishes of families in the western countryside, such as the Sukun area, are inherently sweet, and the sweetness of Luodian's braised mutton is exactly what is needed to this degree, without being considered too sweet. When a bowl of steaming braised mutton is brought in from the door of the dining room, you can smell a sweet fragrance from afar, which makes your appetite open and your appetite boosted! There was a cook next door to my house named A Xiangbao, who was best at making this dish.

Clear Soup Fish Balls Fish balls are available everywhere, but the fish balls made by Luodian people are said to contain eggs, yams, and other special ingredients, so they are particularly delicious. They are more tender than tender tofu, and they melt in your mouth. They also have a particularly clean white color and a clear soup with no impurities, which cannot be matched by those made elsewhere. People find them lovely to look at. This is truly an edible beauty, matching the sentence used to describe a lustful person seeing a beautiful woman in front of him: "I can't wait to swallow him in one gulp!" This clear soup fish ball can make a person eat several bowls without getting tired of it.

Braised Sea Eel This sea eel is also called "Baijie" (I don't know if the character "jie" is written this way), and also called "sea eel rat," because it is transformed from a water rat, people say. This kind of fish is only abundant in the western countryside and is not easy to buy in Shanghai or elsewhere. Its advantage is that it has a lot of meat, and the skin and its nearby parts and head are very fatty, especially the cheeks. People who love to eat sea eel love its fat the most. This sea eel is usually braised at home, and it also has its own advantages when cooked white at banquets. This spring, I happened to participate in the Baoshan County civil servants' get-together (?) held in Luodian, and I ate the cheek pieces of white-braised large sea eel at that table, and I sighed at its fat and richness and its worth of praise! (The pronunciation of this fish's name is like "hui". I don't know if the character "eel" is wrong. I haven't had time to check it. Please correct me.)

Smoked Crucian Carp and Smoked Field Chicken The rivers in the western countryside are stagnant water, clear to the bottom, and the fish, shrimp, and aquatic creatures produced are easy to be huge, and the taste is also particularly fresh. The rather large crucian carp is even more fragrant and appetizing after smoking. It must go through the process of frying in oil, so that the fine bones can be eaten together, avoiding the trouble of picking bones. Smoked crucian carp is cooked at home, but the flavor is better than the smoked herring sold in all the tea shops by an unknown amount. As for smoked field chicken, there are street vendors selling it, large in shape and fine in meat; there are also smoked field chicken lungs that can be bought in piles, the delicacy of which can only be compared to chicken tongue, and it would be a shame to eat them all in one breath. Although smoked field chicken and field chicken lungs are not included in formal banquets, they are very suitable for accompanying wine.

Records of the Fleeting Fragrance of the Imperial Scent 234

— Original by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

In the past, we always found it very difficult to see many trees next to any river; the reason was that Chinese people have always not known how to pay attention to the construction of gardens. Ordinary poor people, because they have no money to buy fuel, compete to cut down trees everywhere, so that except for very remote areas, such as Jilin, Heilongjiang, etc., there are almost no forests in the mainland of China; even rows of trees are rare. But on the left and right of this long river, there are very neat rows of trees planted; drooping down like clusters of green threads, the willows gently fluttered on the water, and in the middle came peach blossoms blooming like red brocade, this scene was truly lovely.

When the Empress Dowager saw such a beautiful scenery, how could she let it go lightly? She insisted on ordering the car to stop so that she could get out of the car and take a small walk. Of course, no one could dissuade her will, so this yellow train stopped in the middle of the road. Everyone on the train who had duties had to follow her down. But getting out of the car did not mean free movement; only the Empress Dowager and a few of us female attendants could walk around at will. After standing upright on the train for a long time, this kind of slight exercise was really necessary. Because the rest of the people had to stand respectfully to the Empress Dowager according to the original rules of the palace; however, those eunuchs could also run back and forth. Eunuchs could not be regarded as people, so they could be allowed to be free. Only those accompanying ministers suffered, standing like clay sculptures and wood carvings, their eyes unable to look around, but must always look at the Empress Dowager, so that when the Empress Dowager had something to say to someone, this person could immediately walk up. Notice of Amendment to the Gold Exchange Business Rules 236

Having examined the Ministry's order to change to the standard, all Article 47 of the business rules of this office has been amended. If the goods are not delivered by the end date of all fixed-term sales and purchases from the December period, this article shall be followed. In addition to submitting a request to the supervisor to forward it to the Ministry of Industry and Finance for record, this is hereby notified. Article 47 For fixed-term sales and purchases, if the goods are not delivered by the end date, the settlement shall be based on the standard gold listing price listed by the Central Bank on the same day. The above-mentioned standard gold price is calculated based on the Central Bank's customs gold unit listing on the same day, which is based on the London pure gold price calculated according to the Central Bank's shilling listing (Shanghai 978 fineness market average gold ten taels (that is, one note) equals London pure gold 9.82607 ounces). In addition to the December transactions that have been done since September 17, all established fixed-term sales and purchases shall be handled in accordance with the above-mentioned article when the December period is transferred on the 15th of this month. If there is no transfer and cash is available for payment, the delivery shall be made in accordance with the regulations. In the event that the goods are not delivered by the end date, the old regulations shall still be followed.

The calculation method of the standard gold price of the Central Bank is as follows:

The pure gold price in London today is 142 shillings and 1 pence, converting pence to 1.705 pence. Each market average gold ten taels (978 fineness) is equal to London pure gold 9.82607 ounces. Multiply 9.82607 by 1.705, which equals 16.753.4 pence. The Central Bank's listing today is 1 shilling and 5 pence and 375/10000, which equals 17 pence and 375/10000. Divide 16.753.4 by 17.375, which equals a standard gold price of 964.2 yuan.

Rumors Trigger Bond Market Decline 239

Far-term "Regular Six" Bonds Drop One Yuan and One Jiao

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange experienced sudden market fluctuations. Initially, the market was weak and listless. In the afternoon session, rumors arose, causing unnecessary panic. The rampant activities of bandits in Sichuan province seemed undeniable. The news from the exchange only surfaced in the afternoon session. Many blindly followed, swayed by the tide without understanding the underlying reasons, and sold off their holdings. Such individuals are easily deceived. Even if there is a small upside in the future, the rebound will be limited. It is advisable to exercise caution. The overall trend yesterday was mainly downward. The market opening in the morning saw mixed gains and losses, with more declines than gains, but the magnitude was minimal. Only the No. 11 counter saw more buying activity. In the second session, prices continued to decline by two or three jiao uniformly. Most of the selling came from retail investors. The afternoon opening continued the decline of two or three jiao in the previous session. After the salt tax, the market rebounded by about one jiao, but remained chaotic and fluctuating. At the close, rumors suddenly surfaced, causing many to sell off their holdings without understanding the situation. The No. 78 counter saw the most aggressive selling. The sellers were mostly out-of-town investors. The floor traders, already holding short positions, took advantage of the opportunity to amplify the trend, leading to an irrational sell-off. Initially, the decline was minimal, but it intensified, with the far-term "Regular Six" bonds dropping by one yuan and one jiao, demonstrating the intentions of the floor traders. Given this, there is likely to be another wave of fluctuations in the future. The market results showed declines ranging from two or three jiao to two yuan and a half, almost entirely occurring during the closing session. The total turnover was 9,635,000 yuan. Futures Wheat Fluctuation Unpredictable 250

Currently, the central force in the wheat market is the flour market, so the prosperity or decline of the market depends on flour sales. Spot transactions were suspended due to the high production prices. Rebound goods were priced 0.1 yuan higher. Later, 200 tons of Saigon rice for October were shipped inland and 100 tons were shipped to the local market, with prices ranging from 4.6 yuan to 4.65 yuan, about 0.05 yuan higher than the previous market.

North-South Goods: Sun-Dried Longan Meat Falls Another Three Yuan 252

The price of sun-dried longan meat from Xiamen has been falling frequently recently. In previous years, the price of Hainan goods was higher than that of Xiamen, but this year, due to limited production, it was difficult to equalize supply and demand, and the price was higher than that of sun-dried meat. Therefore, the sales of Xiamen goods have been gradually increasing, but prices have been difficult to improve. Yesterday, the numbered shops continued to open more than 100 boxes, and the price fell another 3 yuan. The market price may stabilize somewhat at this point.

Free Talk

Yearning and Reality 253

— Hua Zi

Because he knew my recent living situation was not good, a classmate from several years ago (but who had also been estranged for several years) came to my humble abode one evening, saying he had found a position for me, with decent pay. He then left a letter of introduction, telling me to see a certain Mr. So-and-so the next morning. He said, "I feel you are someone who deserves a better life, and the people in my family all say you are a 'good' person, and they kept urging me to pay attention to you. Now, fortunately, I have succeeded." Although my heart was not exactly leaping for joy, as if I had been unemployed for a long time and suddenly found work, his sincere goodwill could not but move me.

I went to ask and found out it was just about writing articles. And it wasn't some special assignment or long-term engagement, but just writing articles to the extent that every publication has submission guidelines at the back. I wasn't exactly disappointed, because I hadn't had much expectation to begin with. I understood very well that my long-estranged classmate studied engineering, and he had been slightly fooled. But his being slightly fooled wasn't because someone deliberately deceived him. He himself didn't realize he had been fooled; on the contrary, he felt immense joy, feeling that he had done something for an old friend. Life is fleeting, how many times can one experience such joy?

People in the world can generally be divided into two types. One is born to be deceived, and the other is born with a skeptical nature, who, even if not necessarily deceiving others, at least doesn't easily get deceived. The former are the so-called simpletons, overly "honest folks," or at least those with a bit of a simple air; the latter often manifest as free and unrestrained thinkers, skeptics. An extreme example of the former would be Mr. Quixote, and the latter can be found in abundance in late 19th-century Russian novels.

The world's successful people also carry a bit of the simpleton's air. Because the world itself is an adventure, if one is suspicious to the left and right, where is there hope of success? The same goes even more so for love. The former see love as a second life, the latter see it as a game. But those who get the greatest taste of love are, of course, the former. Anatole France's novel "Thaïs," its protagonist Paphnutius, is a strict ascetic, but for a dancer Thaïs, he even abandons his faith; but it is he, not Nicias, who obtains the essence of love and tastes the true meaning of life.

The greatness and happiness of those easily deceived! Only they can taste the true flavor of life, the meaning of love. No wonder someone said, "Those who have passed through the youth and prime of life and reached old age should quietly reflect on the past, and they will only regret that they were never deceived in their love life, and never regret being deceived even once."

Postscript to "A Lohan Born from a Clam Shell" 254

— Chen Zizhan

Yesterday I finished writing the article "A Lohan Born from a Clam Shell," and today I remembered that the Qing dynasty Yongne Jushi's "Zhi Wen Lu," volume three, has a section called "Buddha Pearl in a Clam."

The story of the "Buddha Pearl in a Clam" goes like this:

In the fifth month of the year Yiwei during the Qianlong reign, there was a severe drought in Jiangnan, and the water in Chaohu Lake in Chaoxian County also dried up, and boats could not move. One night, the moonlight was very good. A fisherman suddenly saw a cool breeze coming from the bow of his boat, the water was only a little over a foot deep, and it seemed like something was breathing there, but he couldn't find it. So he raised the small sail on his boat and went with the wind. By dawn, he had traveled over a hundred li, the wind stopped, and the water was dry again, and the boat couldn't move. He saw a large clam, as big as a wooden basin, very shiny, and he felt strange, so he opened the clam shell and found a Buddha pearl inside, with eyebrows, eyes, and body, nothing missing, and it glowed every night. He took this large clam to a jewelry shop to consign it for sale, and it happened that a tributary envoy from a Western country was there at the time. When he saw it, he was very fond of it and was willing to pay 30,000 taels of silver to buy it. Unexpectedly, the fisherman was greedy and hoped for a higher price, so he delayed for a long time and did not sell it. Later, he went to ask the envoy again, and the envoy said, "If you had wanted to sell it to me before, I would have doubled the price, but now it's not worth a penny." The fisherman was shocked and asked him, "Why were you willing to pay a high price before, but now you say it's not worth a penny?" He said, "Before, the clam pearl was very good and could be cultivated. If you nourished it with medicine, it could still grow bigger. Now the clam is dead, it's just a carved thing for people to admire." The fisherman still carried the clam to the jewelry shop to sell, and only got 500 cash.

This is of course another myth.

Circulating Libraries and Youth 255

— Fu Hongliao

Literature gives young people such a beautiful vision. However, when any young person begins to step into the confines of literature, there is not one who does not feel lost and at a loss. That is to say, when a young person steps from beautiful fantasy into practice, they are hindered in their minds by questions of literary schools, paths, which famous works should be read to benefit their initial learning, or the relationship between the selection of books and the times. Or, they even go to the bookstore and, facing the dazzling array of books, do not know which one to buy. All of this is a common worry for young people who love literature and are learning it, and this worry has been inherited from the May Fourth Movement until now.

What is the reason for this phenomenon? Of course, we cannot blame a young person for not having the talent to choose. What we should blame is our own literary world, and those writers who are recognized or consider themselves to have a considerable history and responsibility in the literary world! The inheritance that young people should get in the literary system (this is not the same as the inheritance mentioned in the "Literary Monthly") is indeed too meager, or even non-existent. If young people want to read a relatively systematic literary history or a book on literary theory, they will find several different facts and theories in the books (this fact can often be seen in the questions and answers of young people in this newspaper's reading column). If they want to read some world masterpieces, they will also find many translation sentences that they cannot understand in the books. What they see in some publications is only the struggle of opinions and disguised criticism. They want to obtain some experience from famous writers on the cultivation of learning literature, as well as sincere instructions on literature, or notes of writers' research on literature (such as Notebook), which is as elusive as fantasy. These reasons are all elements that damage the vitality of the entire literary world, and will also affect the question of "why there are no great works produced in the literary world." Old writers have forgotten the hardships of their own success, and have completely forgotten about young people. The new forces in the literary world are not seen to be produced, and the old writers are inevitably constrained by age, resulting in the entire literary world becoming anemic, and so-called other miscellaneous diseases, such as "literary revival," are also rising at the same time. The future is indeed unimaginable!

From this phenomenon, we find that "the literary world needs young people, and young people need guidance!" This is not only true for young people who love literature, but also for young people in universities!

In the first issue of the third volume of the "Literary Monthly," there is an article "University Literature," which is a communication from a university's literature department. There is a very realistic description, saying that literary people in a literature department hardly know literature. The reason is that it is too indifferent and irrelevant to the Chinese literary world. Although they also read many world literature books, they themselves cannot say what they are doing and some of the true meanings of literature. Although they know that the literature department is engaged in literary work, in fact, it is difficult for such talents to come from the literature department. It can be seen how lost young people are in literature, and at the same time how much they need beneficial guidance!

At present, in order to remedy this deficiency, I think we should imitate the kind of organized and systematic "circulating libraries" established in Japan.

"Circulating libraries" are bookstores in Japan that specialize in renting literary books and magazines. For a monthly fee of three yuan, they subscribe to a "circulating" book, and they will send a book every three days. No matter what great work it is, the title is chosen by oneself, and ten books can be read every month.

This method is indeed very beneficial to young people. On the one hand, it can save young people from the heavy burden of book fees, and at the same time, it can urge and increase young people's desire to read. It is indeed worth imitating.

There have been "circulating libraries"-style bookstores in China, but what they rent to young people are some knight-errant and Zhang Henshui-style novels. There is simply not a single new literary book. Therefore, at present, we feel that new literary rental bookstores in the "circulating libraries" style are very necessary. Our method is to be run by many people who have made contributions and have cultivation in literature, and to choose truly valuable literary books in the world. A form should be issued to those who rent books, so that they can fill it out. For young people who are just entering the garden of literature, we can choose a systematic book on literary research for them. Send it to them to read, so that they will not feel so confused about literature. Moreover, in this current society of economic depression, it is even more necessary to reduce the burden of books!

Of course, we do not advocate that young people study literature rigidly, but this method will at least be very beneficial to "beginners"!

Translation is Popular Again This Year 256

— Hei Ying

Translated works were once regarded as "matchmakers" and have been looked down upon ever since. You can tell by how few Chinese translations there are. As for magazines that are entirely composed of translated works, it goes without saying that they cannot be seen.

But this year, the situation has changed a bit.

First, "Literature" came up with a special translation issue. "Planned translation is necessary; at the same time, it is also necessary to break the air of contempt for translation." From these words, we express deep sympathy for the painstaking efforts of publishing a special translation issue. However, is it enough to just have one magazine publish a special issue?

Then, after half a year, "Translation" appeared.

Regarding "Translation," some people have already talked about it, so I will skip it here.

Following "Translation," "World Literature" appeared.

This is another publication that focuses on translation, with the purpose of "introducing the literature of various countries, estimating its value for world literature, that is, new literature; publishing works whose content or form can be used as a resource; taking an absolutely objective attitude to explore the path of Chinese literature to world literature" (see the inaugural speech).

Leaving aside its verbose inaugural speech; just looking at the content of its inaugural issue, I think this is a publication worth introducing.

I admire writers who can write excellent works; I sometimes even admire those who can translate great foreign masterpieces very well. This kind of hard work is sometimes more difficult than creation, and even requires a kind of low-energy brute force. You cannot say that a masterpiece by Shakespeare is ultimately not a Chinese work and therefore ignore it; on the contrary, introducing the works of Tolstoy, Gorky, and Zola to China clearly has its significance.

Especially for those of us who are engaged in writing, it is good to be able to find something to learn from in their works.

However, the facts show us that Chinese translations are often not welcomed, because some of them are really incomprehensible. Once such unfaithful translations become numerous in the market, they make people get a headache as soon as they hear the word translation. "Throwing away food because one choked on it" is not good. There are some people who can translate good things, but the general public does not have the patience to choose, and so translation has suffered a bit of misfortune.

At the time of the inaugural issue of "Translation" and "World Literature," I hope that they will strive to make it perfect in terms of content; what to translate and how to translate must be carefully considered. If it can change the current attitude of the public, then the so-called "magazine year" will have made some contribution after all.

Also, "Modern" has also published a special issue on American literature, making the voice of translation even louder. May more foreign masterpieces be introduced to China from now on, I am afraid that the progress of creation also depends on this to some extent.

Village Chief (Part 2, Section 10) 257

— Wang Renshu

The people in the village heard about Dong Quezi. They all hid. Shanfu smoked a good amount of opium at Aji's house and walked from the head of the village. He walked along, singing Meng Jiangnu. He didn't know what had happened in the village. Why was he being attacked? He didn't see anyone returning from working in the mountains or fields. He sang and sang until he reached Cuiluting Pavilion. Suddenly, more than a dozen hands stretched out from the pavilion, grabbing his chest, grabbing his hands, and pulling his legs. Shanfu was immediately tied up by those yellow uniforms.

"What, what? Are you robbing in broad daylight?" Shanfu was startled, and then he understood what was going on. But he still shouted in a pompous manner.

"Robbing? Calling you to training." The squad leader stood up from the wooden beam in the pavilion. "Okay, now we have you to make up the numbers. We don't need the village chief to ask for people anymore."

"Haha!" Shanfu laughed. "Are you drafting soldiers? Why didn't you tell me earlier? I have nothing to do. I'm very willing to learn how to drill." He said, loosening his right hand, took out a cigarette, and sent it to the squad leader's mouth, "What's your honorable surname?"

"My surname is Hong." The squad leader responded weakly.

"Your full name." Shanfu was full of flattery.

"My given name is Le." The squad leader couldn't help but soften his tone.

Shenbao Local Supplement

Talks

Filial Piety Paper 258

— Feng

The words "filial son" originally have several interpretations: (1) A filial son is when parents show filial piety to their son, not when the son shows filial piety to his parents, this is called a filial son, (2) A filial son is only filial in words, so it is called a "filial mouth." Truly, these words are already "old sayings," so let's not talk about them, but it's always "filial son."

Yesterday, I happened to see a thick obituary on a friend's desk. I opened it and looked at it. From important figures in the national government (except for Sun Yat-sen, who did not write an inscription) to famous figures in Shanghai, there were many praises that they uttered to the extreme! It was really amazing. I repeatedly praised, filial son! Filial son!

Later, I looked for his career in the biography, but I couldn't find any of his great achievements. It just said that he had done his best in public welfare undertakings and had made no small contribution to the revolution, etc., empty words. Ah! It was even more amazing. Such a character was actually praised by everyone. It was really amazing.

Later, I pondered the reason, and it turned out that the father became noble because of the son. It was also a way to show off relatives and make a name for oneself. But, but... if the son is not raised well, where would there be such achievements to honor the ancestors? Therefore, the father becomes noble because of the son, and the son also becomes noble because of the father. A non-filial son cannot achieve this.

Therefore, I suspected that the two previous interpretations of the words "filial son" might still have errors. Now everyone doesn't talk about filial piety, and everyone has a headache when they talk about filial sons. Therefore, looking at the facts, we only see "filial piety paper" and don't see filial sons. Therefore, rather than saying that he is a filial son, it is more accurate to say that he is a "filial piety paper."

Osmanthus Blossoms 259

— Shucheng

The maple leaves, as if having drunk too much wine, are drunk with flushed faces, and the thin yellow willow leaves are driven down from the increasingly weakened mother branches, piece by piece, by the merciless west wind, lying horizontally on the sidewalk where passersby tread on them, sighing with their heads lowered!

The sky appears strangely solemn. The evening wind is blowing rustlingly, carrying the sound of galloping horses and men! I walk alone in the autumn wilderness, every cell in my body is contracting; at this moment, I am really a little frightened!

The osmanthus flowers have been blown open by the west wind, emitting a rich fragrance! It is planted in a corner of the southeast side of the backyard; next to it are several withered willows. In the hazy twilight, there are two or three children searching for the "chirping, chirping" little bugs among the tiles and wall crevices.

My mother, holding my clever third sister's hand, walks out from the back door, her face full of smiles, showing extreme kindness; pointing to the osmanthus tree in full bloom, she says to me, "This was planted by your grandfather!"

"It was the year after this house was built." She added a footnote, pointing to her own house.

I have never seen my grandfather: the words "hand-planted" were a bit incomprehensible to my weak brain at that time. However, my fondness for osmanthus flowers developed from picking their petals, drying them in the sun, storing them in bottles, pickling them with salt, and then using them to make tea, which I found fragrant and delicious! So, when it came to the time of the winter solstice or the New Year, the neighbors all liked to come to my house to drink "osmanthus tea."

This was five years ago, and I haven't forgotten it at all; now, when I think back to it, it seems like it was just yesterday! But time is a bit like a thief, imperceptibly slipping past our heads, bodies, and fingers. Now, I have put on the crown of "adulthood," causing me to drift everywhere, suffering the cold eyes of people, and tasting enough of the sourness and bitterness of the world! Ah, my wandering wanderer! My mind is like duckweed; unable to find support, unable to find comfort!

The red maple leaves and the thin yellow willow leaves are falling down with the west wind in rhythm again, the osmanthus flowers in the campus are emitting a rich fragrance, but; what about my home, which is five hundred miles away?

People Who Fly Over Walls 260

— Xin Zi

This year is a year of revival of the old ways. Not only are men and women not allowed to touch hands, but the other reflections of this are also bizarre and abound. For example, a few years ago, there was a public search for people who could fly over walls, but the result was disappointing. Not only were there no people who could fly over walls, but there weren't even any applicants. This made that talent-seeking adult very unhappy, and he sighed that the national martial arts had been lost.

According to the precedents of "Seven Heroes and Five Gallants," "The Cases of Judge Shi," "The Cases of Judge Peng," and other martial arts novels, those heroes who flew over walls were mostly on the side of the "Qing Tian" (upright judge) and helped to eliminate harm for the people. To put it more openly, they were the "semi-immortals" who had seen through the world and did not seek fame or profit. They could ride the clouds and mist, and they had flying swords and other magical treasures. They often did not hesitate to start killing in order to uphold justice.

Could it really be that the national martial arts had been lost? Logically, isn't it the time for those heroes who have no use for their martial arts to devote themselves to serving the country and honoring their ancestors? But the result was disappointment. Not even one applicant appeared. This is probably not because the heroes of today are more noble than the heroes in the novels and do not seek prominence, but because of the "loss of national martial arts."

This year is different. What could not be found a few years ago has now appeared automatically. Not only can they fly over walls, but they can also make themselves invulnerable to swords and spears. Even if a pistol is used, the bullets cannot penetrate their bodies. And according to what he told the interviewer, he not only knows these two things, but he also knows flying swords and acupressure.

According to a friend who had visited him, the hero is indeed a very handsome young man. He wears a suit, a silk shirt, and coffee-colored dancing shoes. His hair is combed neatly, and he probably has a layer of snow cream on his face. He keeps smoking cigarettes. If he didn't tell you, no one would think that such a dandy type of person is an invulnerable hero.

Perhaps it is really because the times have progressed that such a decoration is completely different from the impression that martial arts novels give me, but when I think that novels (especially martial arts novels) are mostly castles in the air built by writers, I feel relieved. Therefore, it is too superficial to say that a hero's decoration should not be so beautiful. Moreover, the Peking opera based on old novels is not like this. For example, once I watched "Tian Ba Baisan," the hero who played Huang Tianba changed his clothes three times, and all three sets of clothes were so new and beautiful, and he also wore a sparkling diamond ring on his hand. Can it be said that such a extraordinary hero should not be dressed so beautifully?

Therefore, the conclusion that being dressed beautifully means not being a hero is too ridiculous, but the fact that Chinese martial arts have not been lost is what makes many people rejoice.

Contradictions 261

— Yuan Zhi

"Are humans destined to live in contradictions forever?"

Whenever the night is hazy outside the window and the city's pulse temporarily stops beating, when I am lonely, keeping company with the burnt-out white candle, gazing at the flickering candlelight on the white wall, this question is like a regular customer, visiting me again.

As usual, I furrow my brow, grab my disheveled hair, and freeze. Naturally, I believe that contradictions can make the path of life more accurate and faster. But sometimes - and often - they will inevitably hinder life, making it take detours, or even go backwards.

Right now, the contradictions in life are making me too painful.

When it's lively, I often feel noisy and disgusted, but when it's calm, I often feel lonely.

When I lived in my hometown, it was really boring and monotonous, like a dormant worm, eagerly hoping to go to the city to be active; but when I got to the city, the disturbance and chaos

Page 23

The appearance made me uneasy, and I often missed the beautiful hometown.

Like ordinary people, in the hot summer, when the sun is scorching above my head and sweat is flying, I really hate it and think it's better to be in winter. But when winter really comes, the north wind howls, the snow flies, and it's so cold that my nose almost falls off, I get the idea that it would be better to be a little hotter in the summer.

The most painful thing is not the things mentioned above; but the contradiction between emotion and reason is what makes it most impossible for me to resolve.

Often, because of the pressure of life, I want to recklessly do something despicable in order to seek material enjoyment and a high position. When I think about it again, reason immediately puts on a solemn face and scolds me unceremoniously. He teaches me that I should have a strict life, walk on a straight path, and seek light through constant effort.

Most of my time can be said to have slipped by in the contradictions of ideals and the contradictions of behavior, as well as the contradictions of ideals and behavior. However, to this day I still cannot definitively answer this question:

"Are humans destined to live in contradictions forever?"

Remnants 262

Friendship 263

— Dongdong

I didn't close my eyes all night, perhaps due to excessive excitement. Truly, friend! After your mother told me about you, I was so happy I didn't know how to express it. For your mother, of course, it was like regaining a beloved treasure; however, she couldn't help but shed a few tears. The sudden joy stirred up her past sorrows, and she worries that your strong personality will be unwilling to accept her earnest advice and return home. I comforted her for a while and, at her request, promised to come here and find you today.

On the way home, your shadow never left my mind. Indeed, your departure that time was a bit too hard-hearted. We are old friends of many years. I sympathize with your character, your hidden sadness; I feel that your character is not something that ordinary, vulgar people can understand, but I truly don't understand why you treat me the same as everyone else. In any case, you should consider this a fault and reproach yourself for it. Moreover, you abandoned your white-haired mother and young siblings.

When the clock struck six, I rubbed my tired eyes, propped up my weary limbs, washed my face with cold water, braced myself, and rushed to catch the early boat to Village C.

Arriving at Village C, I quickly grabbed a sturdy man and inquired about the route here. He stretched out his fingertip and pointed for a long time. I just responded with "uh-huh, uh-huh" to his voice, but I was actually very confused. The number of right and left turns left me not knowing which road to take first. The burly man probably realized I couldn't remember all the turns at once, so he finally told me to go straight ahead on the left side, and then ask passersby at the intersection. I followed his directions, walked for a full hour, asked several people, and finally arrived at your quaint residence.

As luck would have it, you had just gone out. I asked your neighbor, and she said you rarely go out. You usually just sit at home all day. She didn't know what made you go out today, causing you to temporarily abandon this old house.

I have been waiting here for almost three hours. I can't wait any longer. I have to go back. If I'm late, I'm afraid I'll miss the boat and make my family worry. Now, I have written so many words to you. It is my sincere hope that you will come home!

Gambling and Entertainment 264

— Yugong

Since human society evolved to the point where people are dissatisfied with material enjoyment, human desires have grown, and their gambling spirit has become stronger. Therefore, they want to get rich effortlessly in the shortest possible time from their impoverished circumstances. As a result, gambling for profit has become a traditional concept. Especially in this present society where the rich get richer and the poor get poorer, the trend of gambling is at its peak.

Although gambling was not completely absent in ancient times, judging from the historical fact that Confucius, the sage, considered gambling as extracurricular activity to be encouraged among his students during the Warring States and Spring and Autumn periods, it is clear that the ancients did not intend to get rich from it. (The Analects records: "The Master said, 'Is it not better to play chess than to do nothing all day long?'" Confucius believed that gambling all day was better than being idle all day. However, nowadays, even playing chess is used to make a small fortune, truly the morals of the world are deteriorating, it is unbearable to look back!)

What is most puzzling is that for all entertainment activities, if there is no money involved in winning or losing, people think it's boring and uninteresting. Isn't this strange? Four old women play mahjong! They naturally think they are having fun, but if someone declares that this is just for fun, then they are unwilling to sit together. Does this mean that entertainment and gambling cannot be separated? The more you think about it, the more inexplicable it becomes.

Foreigners' horse racing, dog racing, and jai alai games, on the surface, are clearly games for the entertainment of the audience; but they are for gambling. One side sets up these games to collect commission as a business, and the other side buys tickets and gambles in the hope of making a small fortune. Foreigners understand the weaknesses of human nature in society. They commercialize entertainment activities and use them to do business, which is something that our ancient Chinese sages could not even imagine.

However, the reason why there are people who set up gambling for profit and people who gamble in the hope of getting rich is because the social system makes people dissatisfied with material enjoyment. If there is no gambling in society one day, it must be when a social system that allows people to be satisfied with material enjoyment arrives.

Punishment 265

— Ms. Jiong

In the morning, a round sun had already hung in the sky, and birds chirped sharply, seeming to be immersed in mutual joy. All around was quiet.

People were all in sweet slumber. In order to fight for life, I had to abandon my comfortable sleep.

Home
